Shanghai's Film Industry 126

— Compiled by Editor Zhengzhu

(Part 34 of Shanghai's Industrial and Commercial Overview)

(1) Introduction: The Chinese film industry has existed for nearly twenty years. Over these twenty years, the majority (90%) of film studios and management companies have been concentrated in Shanghai. Therefore, the situation of this industry in Shanghai can be representative of the whole country. The Chinese film industry, like other national industries, has suffered from the oppression of foreign films for twenty years and still struggles beneath their shadow, facing countless crises that are difficult to describe. The main reasons for its survival and continued hope for significant development are advancements in technology and government encouragement.

The film industry in Shanghai can be broadly divided into three categories: production, management, and cinemas. There has been no foreign investment in film production. Although some foreigners have attempted to establish factories in Shanghai, they have ultimately failed due to various reasons. Management and cinemas, however, are mostly controlled by foreigners. For example, the "Big Eight" American film companies in Shanghai almost completely control the film distribution business, dominating the entire market.

This article aims to outline the history and current status of film production and management, incorporating cinemas into the film market section. They will be described separately below.

(2) History: In 190X, American Mr. Blashki organized the Asia Film Company in Shanghai, producing the films "Empress Dowager Cixi" and "The Unfortunate Son." In 191X, American Mr. Ischler traveled to China during the thriving period of modern drama. Ischler collaborated with people in the modern drama industry, utilizing the actors, costumes, and sets of modern drama to produce the films "Zhuangzi Breaking Open the Coffin" and "The Unjust Soul of the Black Register." However, the plots were unremarkable, and the acting was poor. The only reason for their popularity was the novelty of motion pictures. Both companies closed after the outbreak of the European War.

In 191X, the Commercial Press established a film department, engaging in the production of educational and scenic short films, marking the beginning of domestic film production. The following year, Universal Pictures Corp. of America came to Shanghai to produce films, hoping to compete with the Commercial Press. In 191X, Gu Xianfu, Guan Haifeng, and others organized the New Asia Company, producing "Red Pink Skull." However, Du Yu and others organized the Shanghai Company, producing "Sea Oath." The following year, Zheng Zhegu (deceased), Zheng Zhengqiu (deceased), Zhang Shichuan, Zhou Jianyun, Ren Jinping, and others organized the Star Film Company, producing short comedic films, followed by the film "Retribution is Clear." This marked the beginning of formal film production companies in China.

In 192X, more companies were established, including Great China, Great Wall, Lily, Great Shanghai, and New China. In 192X, the Tianyi Company was established by the Shao Zuiweng brothers. At that time, film companies emerged like bamboo shoots after rain. Seventeen more companies were subsequently established, including Shenzhou, United Friends, and New Youth. In the same year, Great China and Lily merged to form Great China Lily. By this time, the film industry was gradually prospering. In 192X, the film department of the Commercial Press was reorganized into the Guoguang Company. Ren Jinping left Star and formed his own Newcomer Company. In addition, thirteen more companies were established, including Minxin and Huaju. Although there were many companies in these years, they rose and fell quickly. Most of them closed down shortly after, or only existed in name without producing any films. As a result, internal conflicts in the film industry intensified, plunging the entire industry into a chaotic era. Since the establishment of the Film Censorship Board, small companies were gradually eliminated. After 192X, the industry began to get back on track. Great China Lily and Minxin merged again, officially establishing the Lianhua Film Company on October 15, 193X, revitalizing the film industry.

During this period, a few foreigners attempted to establish film production plants in China. For example, in 192X, the British American Tobacco Company had a film investment plan. In 193X, a Sino-foreign joint venture established the China First Company. In the same year, a foreigner named Betly Conepson attempted to establish a Sino-foreign company. However, due to the well-organized domestic film industry, foreign capital could not penetrate it. Government guidance also played a significant role.

According to the Ministry of Industry's report, there were 37 film companies in Shanghai by 193X. Among them, only Star, Lianhua, and Tianyi were relatively large. Most companies had suspended operations due to the January 28th Incident. By 193X, only a dozen companies remained. In 193X, Yi Hua was established. In 193X, more companies were established, including Diantong, Xinhua, and Yucheng. In the current year, Diantong and Yucheng have closed, and new companies such as Xinhua and Culture have been established. According to Lianhua Company statistics, there are currently eleven film companies in Shanghai, with seven actually producing films. This is a general overview of the film production industry in Shanghai.

Most of the existing technical personnel in the Shanghai film industry, such as cameramen and set designers, are not specialists. Their current achievements are mainly derived from experience. Notable achievements include the production of sound films and Star Company's attempt at color films. In 192X, imported sound films were introduced to China, and major cinemas in Shanghai gradually screened them. Film studios collectively considered producing sound films. However, due to high costs and lack of talent, it was difficult to implement. Therefore, they first produced phonograph records for dubbing, such as Lianhua's "Wild Grasses and Idle Flowers," Star's "Singing Girl Red Peony," and United Friends' "Yu Meiren." Later, Chen Qiufeng and others organized a company to go to Japan to produce "After the Rain, Clear Sky." In 193X, Tianyi began producing sound films with sound-on-film technology, "Singing Arena Spring." This marked the beginning of sound films with sound directly on the film in China. Star Company also sent Professor Hong Shen to the United States to purchase sound equipment and hired two sound engineers, producing films such as "Flesh Market." At the same time, more and more Chinese people invented sound equipment, such as Shi Shiqing's "Eastone," Yan Hemian's "Hemingtone," and Zhu Qingxian's "Qingxian Type." With this, sound recording technology no longer relied entirely on foreigners, and the production of sound films became more widespread. Currently, there are eight companies in Shanghai that produce and sell sound equipment, but most are used by cinemas. In 193X, Star Company, recognizing the popularity of color films, filmed a portion of "Tears and Laughter Marriage" in color. However, due to poor technology and high costs, there have been no successors. The Star authorities have also abandoned this attempt. Other advancements, such as the Wan brothers' invention of self-made animated cartoons, are also a significant step forward in film technology.

It is also necessary to mention the import and competition of foreign films. Foreign films have been well-received in Shanghai since their arrival in 190X. A Spaniard named Remas first opened the Rosam' Vo toria (now renamed New Central) cinema in Shanghai, as well as Summer Peck, Aipro, and others. At that time, there were almost no domestic films. Not only were all films screened foreign films, but all cinemas were also opened by foreigners. Later, with the establishment of Star Company and the emergence of domestic films, the Central Company was organized to manage five cinemas: Central, New Central, Carde, International, and Empire, exclusively screening domestic films. At that time, the business comparison between domestic and foreign films was only 5 to 95. In 192X, various American film companies, such as Paramount and Fox, came to China to establish branches, controlling the Shanghai film market. In the same year, sound films began to be screened in China. However, the result was that, on the one hand, due to the progress of domestic films, and on the other hand, due to language barriers between Chinese and foreign languages, business was not as good as in the silent film era. Even first-class cinemas like Nanjing screened domestic films such as "Tears and Laughter Marriage" to attract audiences. In November 193X, foreign film companies united with cinemas such as Grand Guangming, Nanjing, Cathay, Carlton, Summer Peck, and Willie to organize the China Foreign Film Merchants Association, with R. B. Butter as chairman, to find ways to promote business. However, due to the economic downturn and industrial and commercial decline, by 193X, their turnover had decreased by 25% compared to previous years. At the same time, the Chinese government also worked hard to promote domestic films, issuing incentive measures, reducing taxes as much as possible, and increasing foreign film import taxes and inspection fees to show restrictions. Since then, the market for domestic films in Shanghai has slightly increased. However, currently, only Jincheng cinema screens first-class domestic films in Shanghai. The power of foreign films still plays a decisive role.

The market for domestic films is not limited to Shanghai. For example, during the era of martial arts films, they were popular in various Nanyang ports. Some companies even specialized in selling to the five Nanyang territories (British Nanyang, Dutch Nanyang, the Philippines, Siam, and Annam). Recently, the number of cinemas in the mainland has increased, and the market for domestic films has expanded significantly. However, since the crackdown on supernatural martial arts films, the productions in recent years have not been as popular as before with overseas Chinese in Nanyang. Moreover, the Nanyang market is also declining. Therefore, the main business of domestic films is still in Shanghai. However, on the one hand, cinemas screening domestic films in Shanghai still feel that the supply is insufficient. On the other hand, film producers still believe that after a film is screened in Shanghai, there are too few places outside Shanghai where it can be screened, so they still need to lose money. Therefore, they dare not produce too many films. This is indeed a bottleneck in the film business. (To be continued)

Weather Report 127

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated: The area around Shandong and the Yellow River basin are cloudy with localized showers and northeasterly to southeasterly winds. The Yangtze River basin and the East China Sea are cloudy but still fine or may experience thunderstorms with northeasterly to southeasterly winds. There are strong winds in southern Taiwan, and the weather is severe due to a hurricane moving northwest-west. The center of the hurricane was within 60 miles of 20 degrees North Latitude and 119 degrees East Longitude at X PM yesterday, with fierce winds. Also, in the 24 hours before 3 PM yesterday, the local temperature reached a high of 90.5 and a low of 75.0. On the same day last year, the high was 90.9 and the low was 72.1.

Letters to the Editor 128

Dear Editor,

Regarding the report in your newspaper on August 16 concerning the sinking of the Huadong No. 1 fishing boat, we have found it to be inconsistent with the facts. We are writing to clarify the situation and request a correction. The Huadong No. 1 fishing boat docked at our factory's wharf on the 7th but had not yet entered the dry dock for repairs. The accident last night was due to the negligence of the captain, who failed to anticipate the effects of the tide, causing the boat to tilt and take on water. Our factory is not responsible for any accidents that occur to boats we are repairing before they enter the dry dock. However, due to our friendly relationship with the fishing company, we have arranged for workers to pump out the accumulated water, and the boat has been restored to its original condition. We are writing to request that you publish this correction in your newspaper.

Sincerely,

Gongmao Machinery Shipbuilding Factory

August 16

Dear Editor,

We were shocked to read the news in your newspaper about the Huadong fishing boat sinking in front of the Gongmao factory in Pudong. Our fishing boat, Huadong No. 1, was undergoing annual repairs at the Gongmao shipyard after the fishing season ended. Yesterday, the factory needed to use the dry dock for a larger vessel. Therefore, it moved our fishing boat southward. Unexpectedly, the river bottom there was deep on the outside and shallow on the inside, causing the boat to tilt. The hold was flooded with the tide. This morning, the tide receded, and the water was pumped out. The boat is now unharmed. We are concerned that this misinformation may spread. We hereby request a correction.

Sincerely,

Shanghai Huadong Fisheries Company

Eleventh Olympic Games 1936

Grand Event Ends on the 16th The World Games Held Closing Ceremony Yesterday The Five-Ring Flag Lowered Amidst Music and Gunfire The Marathon Tower's Torch Also Extinguished 6,000 Young People from Around the World Depart Separately 129

Central News Agency Special Correspondent, Berlin, 16th - The Eleventh Olympic Games, which began in Berlin on August 1st, proceeded exceptionally smoothly. All events were completed by today. The closing ceremony is scheduled for 5:00 PM today.

Allied Press, Berlin, 16th - The Eleventh International Olympic Games, which gathered 6,000 young warriors from around the world to perform fervent competitions, after opening on August 1st, reached its peak and ended with a solemn closing ceremony at 7:00 PM on the 16th at the Grunewald Stadium. At 7:20 PM, the Marathon Tower trumpets sounded, shaking the distant reaches. Flag bearers from each country carried their national flags and entered the stadium in single file to the accompaniment of marches, lined up in a horizontal row facing the VIP grandstand. International Olympic Committee Chairman Count Latour rose and delivered the closing speech. Next, "The Flame Song" was played. At 7:33 PM, the order to lower the flag was given. The music was melodious, celebratory guns fired in succession, and the five-ring Olympic flag gradually descended. The torch burning on the Marathon Tower also disappeared at some unknown time, causing people to feel a sense of parting. The removed Olympic flag was handed over by the acting mayor of Los Angeles, Mr. Gammonde, to the mayor of Berlin, Mr. Liebel. The three flagpoles bearing the names of Germany 1936, Greece 1896, and Japan 1940 were then arranged with the Greek flag in the center, the German flag on the left, and the Japanese flag on the right, clearly indicating that the next Games would be held in Tokyo. Finally, Team Leader Hiranuma, representing the Japanese Olympic Committee, took the stage to explain the Tokyo Olympic Games and invited all to come early. The applause throughout the stadium was thunderous. Afterwards, the German orchestra sang the Olympic Anthem. After the song ended, the bells rang in succession for five minutes. From this point, the athletes of each country gradually withdrew from the venue. The current Games were declared a complete success, and the event was adjourned at 8:00 PM.

Detailed Account of the Italy-Austria Football Final More Than 160,000 Spectators The Austrian Goalkeeper's Performance Was Outstanding 130

(Central News Agency Special Correspondent, Berlin Radio, 16th) - Yesterday's Italy-Austria football final, held in the main stadium, was the liveliest event since the opening. There were 160,000 spectators. In addition, there were thousands more who could not purchase tickets and stood outside the stadium, listening to the radio broadcast. Its popularity is evident. The stadium's grass was as green as a carpet, and the field was flat and boundless, extremely suitable for running. More than a hundred children were hired around the field to pick up balls, in order to avoid delaying time. The spectators from both countries organized cheering squads, chanting and cheering, and the situation was extremely enthusiastic.

Italy's Victory Certainly Not Accidental

During the match, there was not a minute that was not extremely tense. The performance of both teams was superb. The forwards' attacks and the defenders' blocks were both unique. After 45 minutes of fierce battle, neither side had scored. In the second half, each side scored one goal. In the 30-minute overtime, Italy scored two goals and won. Italy's victory was due to its special strengths and was certainly not accidental. The defense was as solid as a steel wall, and the forwards' attacks were incredibly fast. Especially the left wing's performance was the most outstanding, sharp and extraordinary. Passing and shooting were effortless. The entire team worked together seamlessly.

Austrian Goalkeeper Unmatched Worldwide

Austria was also a strong team and performed very well. Otherwise, the game would not have gone to overtime and they would not have lost by just one goal. The Austrian goalkeeper's skills were praised throughout the stadium. High balls, bouncing balls, whether jumping or lying down, he could save them all. His courage was even more admirable. The two goals conceded were both unavoidable. Spectators said that if a world football team was organized to compete against other planets, forwards and midfielders could be chosen from various countries, which would not be easy, but the Austrian goalkeeper would definitely be selected without any doubt.

Neither Side Scored in the First Half

During the match, both sides were eager to win, and their actions were inevitably excessive, which was regrettable. After the start of the match, Austria took the offensive first, but failed to succeed. Italy then counterattacked. A winger drove along the side. The Austrian midfield and defenders responded and blocked. The ball hovered near the goal. The situation was extremely dangerous. Before long, the Austrian team also showed its power in front of the Italian goal. Fortunately, the shot was inaccurate, avoiding danger. The tense and fierce situation was breathtaking. After 45 minutes of fierce battle, neither side had scored.

Italy Opens the Scoring Team Members Celebrate

After switching sides, both teams were eager to win the championship, and the match became even more exciting. After 24 minutes, the Italian left wing lightly attacked, dribbling the ball to the opponent's goal and kicking it. The Austrian goalkeeper dived and slapped the ball out. The Italian left wing caught up and kicked again. The ball went into the net, opening the scoring. The Italian players shook hands and kissed the left wing. The audience cheered like thunder. After that, the Italian team's momentum was very strong. Austria tried its best to counterattack. Nine minutes before the end, they finally had an opportunity. The left inside forward dribbled the ball and broke through several defenses. Near the opponent's back line, about ten yards from the goal, he lifted his foot and shot. The ball flew straight into the upper left corner of the goal. The Italian goalkeeper thought the ball had gone out of bounds. He was stunned and did not know what to do. The score became 1-1, a tie.

Overtime Ends in Final Victory

The overtime was 30 minutes. In order to take the initiative, Austria launched a major offensive, but still failed. The Italian right wing launched another attack, going straight along the side. When they reached the baseline, they passed the ball to the left wing. After getting the ball, the left wing dribbled up to about five yards from the goal and shot, scoring a goal. Cheers rose again. Austria, losing this goal, had no choice but to try to counterattack. Except for the goalkeeper, all the players crossed the midfield line, trying to recover lost ground. Italy also deployed troops to defend closely. In the last five minutes, Austria shot at the Italian goal three times in a row from about twenty yards away. But all three shots were blocked. This was probably due to carelessness.

British Lord Aberdare Praises the Current World Games 131

National Maritime News Agency, Berlin, August 15th - Lord Aberdare, a member of the International Olympic Committee, told reporters today, "The future success of the Olympic Games seems to be improving day by day. This time in Berlin has been another unparalleled success."

The British sportsman said of the friendship and hospitality of the people of Berlin during the World Games, "I feel that all the people of Berlin participated in this world youth conference with sincerity and friendship."

Regarding British-German relations, Lord Aberdare said that the friendly relations between Britain and Germany are historically very close. Moreover, the two nations have a close relationship in blood. Finally, Lord Aberdare said, "The impression I gained during my short stay in Germany is that all the German people are of one heart and one mind and are striving together under the great leadership. When I visited Chancellor Hitler, I felt that he was one of the most influential people in the German nation. After various conversations, I deeply believe that Germany is sincerely seeking cooperation with Britain to jointly maintain world peace. All European countries should be grateful to Germany, because the German National Socialist Party government opposes communism and clears its influence."

World Games Delegation Diary (Letter 7) - Special Correspondent Feng Youzhen 137

(39) The Olympic Village

The Olympic Village is built near Topsille, 40 kilometers outside Berlin. Although the village's houses were only recently completed, Germany has been planning and building this village for more than ten years. Therefore, the 140-plus acres of land are covered with lush green grass and tall trees, almost like a garden. It is said that after the closing of the World Games, this village will be converted into a barracks. Germans are always so well-planned in whatever they do.

In front of the village, a two-story building in the shape of the Chinese character "人" (person) was built, called the International Building. It can be said to be the headquarters of the village. In addition to the offices, each participating country has an office. There are also post offices, telegraph offices, banks, and shops, with very complete facilities. Therefore, although the village is far from Berlin, the athletes can buy everything they need here without any shortcomings.

The highest administrative officer in the village is the governor, who is supported by many senior officers, soldiers, and youth service corps members. The security and order of the village are maintained by senior officers leading the soldiers, and all services are provided by members of the youth service corps. The members of the youth service corps are all university or high school students who have received special training in advance. They all wear white uniforms and are assigned to the dormitories of various countries according to the foreign languages they speak, representing a neat and generous attitude, and being kind and sincere. The members of the corps serving in the Chinese athletes' dormitory are commanded by officer Kuef Y. Mr. Kuef once served as a consultant in our country and speaks fluent Mandarin. He gets along very well with the athletes.

There is a typing room in the village building, where more than a dozen young women are engaged in typing work. They are always happy to help with any brief requests. Apart from these women, no other women can be found in the village.

There are a total of 178 new houses in the village. Each house and each road is named after a German place name. Each house is hung with a map of the local area, making it easy for athletes from various countries to recognize. The German propaganda method can be called very clever.

The largest building in the village is called the Berlin Building. It is four stories high and also has a basement. It is the dining hall where athletes from various countries gather for meals. There are more than 40 rooms in this building, each with a kitchen in the back. The ingredients used in the kitchen are stored in the basement. When needed, they can be notified by telephone. Each country's dining room has its own national flag. The athletes from Japan, the United States, and Italy are the most numerous, so the dining rooms are also the largest. The Chinese athletes' dining room is next to Bulgaria. Each meal has a different menu and is cooked according to the tastes of each country. The Chinese athletes can eat white rice, one soup, and two dishes for each meal. The taste is very delicious. As for eggs, milk, coffee, and vegetables, they can be enjoyed to the fullest. No one is not satisfied.

The dormitories are all bungalows, with eleven rooms in each building and two people in each room. Not only are they equipped with telephones and bathrooms, but even towels, quilts, toothbrushes, and toothpaste are fully supplied. It can be said to be very thoughtful. Our Chinese athletes occupy buildings 70, 72, 90, and 92, but number 72 is shared with Mexican athletes. Female athletes live separately in the female dormitory, which is far from the village. Male martial arts athletes live in the barracks. In addition, representatives from track and field, basketball, boxing, weightlifting, race walking, and cycling teams all live in the village.

There are two hospitals in the village, one is a general hospital and the other is a specialized hospital. The doctors used are all very famous figures in Germany. The equipment in the hospital is complete and the instruments are new. Many large hospitals in China cannot compare with it. The X-ray in the specialized hospital can clearly show the movement of the heart and stomach. Athletes from various countries take this opportunity to check their bodies. The doctors are overwhelmed with work.

The sports field in the village is not only very large but also has new facilities. The runway is paved with yellow sand, which is hard and moderate, far better than a cinder track. The jumping pit is filled with white sand. The hurdles and high jump frames are also made with the latest methods. Every morning at 5:30, athletes from various countries start practicing. The long-distance running experts from Finland and the short black people from the United States are the most noticeable. There are seven or eight fighting and boxing fields. There are friendly matches every morning and afternoon, attracting many spectators.

From 9 p.m. to 10 p.m., entertainment programs are held in the Hindenburg Building, including songs, dances, movies, and various performances, all of which are wonderful and dazzling. Athletes from various countries can participate freely, like an international gathering. There are more than 300 athletes from the United States. Their costumes are strange, their attitudes are lively and innocent, and they are the most eye-catching in the entire venue. In short, the athletes live in a beautiful environment in the village, leading a regular and interesting life every day. Their spirits and bodies are very happy. After the opening of the Games, they should create more excellent records.

Reform and Construction of China's Sports Policy - Wu Tiecheng 141

Broadcast speech on the establishment of the Shanghai Municipal Sports College

The most basic condition for the development of a country and the rejuvenation of a nation is to improve the function of national cells and develop the superior qualities of the people's intelligence, morality, and physique. The ancient Western philosopher Plato discussed the establishment of an ideal country, requiring its citizens to have four virtues: justice, temperance, wisdom, and courage. Justice is the basis of all virtues, temperance can prevent the indulgence of desires, wisdom can govern the country, and courage can defend the country. The principles of teaching the people by the ancient Chinese sages also did not go beyond these three points:

First, intelligence;

Second, benevolence;

Third, courage. Therefore, it is said, "Intelligence, benevolence, and courage are the universal virtues of the world." These three virtues, from the individual's point of view, are the essential elements for completing one's personality; from the country's point of view, they are even more the essential elements for building and strengthening the country. Therefore, cultivating and developing the superior qualities of intelligence, morality, and physique, or intelligence, benevolence, and courage, is indeed the primary task of teaching the people and building the country. In the process of rejuvenating the nation, those who bear the heavy responsibility of teaching the people and building the country should not neglect or ignore the cultivation of these superior qualities of the people's intelligence, morality, and physique. At the same time, we, as the national cells of the country, if we want to shoulder the great mission of saving the country, preserving its existence, and rejuvenating the nation, should be intelligent and virtuous, and cultivate both literary and military skills, so as to balance the development of the three qualities of intelligence, morality, and physique, and fully promote the universal virtues of intelligence, benevolence, and courage.

Unfortunately, the Confucian scholars of the past misunderstood the true meaning of the holy way, misinterpreted the scope of education, only engaged in recitation, did not attend to practical matters, talked emptily about human nature and reason, did not value practice, loved ease and hated labor, and advocated rejection of advancement, thereby creating a kind of nihilistic and decadent academic style. As a result, the people's will became depressed and the nation declined day by day. The reason for poverty and weakness is indeed a serious step. Since the rise of new studies, Western sports methods have been transplanted to China, and the academic style in various parts of the country has also changed. However, due to errors in sports policy, neither a sound system nor a perfect organization and appropriate training have been established. Some people devoted to sports are also inevitably obsessed with fame and fortune, and immersed in vanity. They usually do not focus on their studies, and when the time comes, they each hold their own opinions, and even make noise and exaggerate, regarding sports as the patent of a few special people, destroying the proper and great significance and function of sports, and having no benefit to the health of the general people, the increase of the productive forces of the entire society, and the self-defense of the country.

Although China has athletes participating in the World Games held in Berlin this time, the results of competing with athletes from various countries in track and field, swimming, soccer, and basketball cannot compete with others. Our purpose in participating in the World Games is not to compete with others for a day's worth of short-term gains. Although we should not be disappointed or discouraged by the result of this disastrous defeat, we must learn from the past and use the stones of other mountains to polish our own jade. What we have observed and felt about the sports policies, sports systems, sports organizations, sports methods, sports training, and sports spirit of various countries cannot but be selectively followed as a reference. We must also deeply reflect on and seek to improve our own shortcomings - no policy, no organization, no method, no training, no effort, no sincerity, no hard work, no cooperation.

Since the European War, the world's sports policies have undergone new changes due to the pressure of the times and the needs of the environment. The wise authorities of various countries have a new understanding of the significance of sports. For example, Italy regards sports as an urgent task for training youth and revitalizing the nation. The Soviet Union regards sports competitions as a "national defense and production examination." Therefore, sports today is no longer the patent of athletes or a recreational pastime. Its scope has become increasingly popular, and it has almost integrated with the entire people. Its purpose is to focus on production and national defense. In addition to strengthening the people's physical and mental health and training ordinary skills, it also provides various training related to increasing production capacity and combat techniques, with the aim of enabling the entire people to have the ability and spirit of long-term labor and national resistance.

China is deeply weak, the people's physique is so frail, the people's spirit is so depressed, the production capacity is so backward, and the foundation of national defense is so weak. Therefore, China's sports policy today must be thoroughly reformed. China's sports experts today should eliminate personal vanity, eliminate the accumulated habits of exaggeration, and not think that they have exhausted the skills of sports by running, jumping, playing, and losing their ambitions. They should deeply understand the trend of modern sports development and its great significance, work hard, practice diligently, and strive upwards, "suffering their minds, laboring their muscles and bones," so as to be able to shoulder the arduous mission of rejuvenating the nation, so that our poor and weak motherland and the precarious national fortune may have the hope of becoming rich and strong and turning around.

In view of this, our city intends to use the existing large sports field to establish a sports college with a relatively complete scale as a test for reforming China's sports policy, based on the principles of national defense, militarization, production, and popularization of sports, and according to the needs of the national reality, to cultivate new and healthy sports teachers to be the guides for training young people across the country. In addition to strengthening the physical fitness of the general public, we can also inspire the spirit of the people and transform the decadent and habitual inferiority of the people, so that the people of the whole country can develop a spirit of perseverance, loyalty, courage, and striving under a sound sports policy, so as to generally improve the productivity of society and enrich the nation's self-defense capabilities, not only to win medals when competing with athletes from various countries, but also to be brave warriors to defend the survival of the country in the critical juncture of national struggle, in order to win and permanently preserve the glory of our nation. August 16, 1936.

Twenty-Three Cultural Organizations Bid Farewell to Students Going Abroad Yesterday; Mayor Wu Presided and Delivered a Farewell Speech; Speeches Also Given by Mu Ouchu, Wang Xiaolai, and Others; Second Group of Students Going to America Scheduled to Set Sail Tomorrow 147

The Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Education and twenty-three organizations including the World Student Association jointly held a farewell ceremony for this year's students going abroad at the municipal government auditorium at 4 p.m. yesterday. Mayor Wu presided over the ceremony and delivered a farewell speech. Wang Xiaolai, Mu Ouchu, and others gave speeches. Student representatives Ms. Shen Yao and Wang Xiangyao and Xu Zongyi gave replies. The atmosphere was very enthusiastic. Details are recorded as follows:

Representatives Present

Included Mayor Wu Tiecheng, Garrison Commander Yang Xiaotian, Shen Yi of the Public Works Bureau, Cai Jingjun of the Public Security Bureau, Jiang Jianbai representing the Municipal Bureau of Education, Zhu Shaoping and Wu Deyin of the World Student Association, Hu Duanxing of Jiaotong University, Du Zuozhou of Jinan University, Qin Mian'an of Guanghua University, Liu Zhanen of Hujiang University, Wang Xiaolai of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Mu Ouchu and Du Yuesheng of the Local Association, Huang Zaoxiong of the Municipal Education Association, Shi Yangnan of the Vocational Education Society, Xu Xinliu of the International Four-Question Research Association, He Zhenya and Wu Zijing of the German-Austrian Alumni Association, Ma Chonggan of Shen Bao, Zai Boqi and Hu Shuyi of Xinwen Bao, Zhu Yixin of Min Bao, Huang Zheheng of Zhonghua Ribao, Chen Dongbai of Jiaoyu Ribao, Zhu Zhiming of Shanghai Xinwenshe, Dong Xianguang of Dalu Bao, Zhu Shaoping of Zhongguo Pinglun Bao, Huang Jingwan of Shangwu, Cheng Shisheng of Zhonghua, Zhao Luqing of Shijie Shuju, and over five hundred students going abroad.

Mayor's Speech

After the music played and everyone took their seats, Mayor Wu delivered a farewell speech, saying briefly: "Today, various cultural organizations in Shanghai are jointly bidding farewell to this year's students going abroad. I am very honored to be the chairman. Shanghai is the hub of communication between China and foreign countries. Every year, students from all over the country going abroad mostly leave from Shanghai, so the people of Shanghai all feel honored. In the past decade, especially in the last four or five years, China has faced the most difficult times in its history. In this time of serious national crisis and economic distress, the number of students going abroad is increasing year by year, with self-funded students accounting for three-quarters of the total. From this, we can see that the Chinese people are aware that building the country and making it prosperous and strong does not depend on fate, but requires intelligence, knowledge, and ability. Therefore, although the people of the whole country are suffering greatly, even when many don't have enough to eat, they are able to take out money to send their children abroad to study. This is undoubtedly a ray of dawn for China's future. From this ray of dawn, we can predict that China's future holds boundless hope. This is the first point. Secondly, in the past, most students studying abroad were studying liberal arts. This year, the total number of students studying abroad is more than 300, and three-quarters of them are studying science and engineering, with liberal arts accounting for only one-quarter. This point can also prove that students studying abroad are able to recognize the current needs of the country. This is the second point. From the above points, we feel that the future of the country is hopeful, and that hope lies in today's youth, who will bear the responsibility for the country's future. If today's youth can wholeheartedly study abroad for the sake of our country and our people, then we should celebrate for the country. In addition, when you go abroad to study, you should not only seek knowledge from books, but also carefully study the ways in which European and American countries have become prosperous and strong. Today's cultural organizations are bidding farewell, and I represent everyone's wishes in offering my best wishes for your success."

Speeches by Guests

Zhang Fayao then gave a speech reporting on the living conditions in European and American countries. Then, Wang Xiaolai gave a speech, in which, in addition to encouraging the students going abroad to work hard in their studies, he also hoped that the World Student Association would report on the situation of the students after they returned to China. After Wang's speech, Mu Ouchu, a veteran of our country's students studying abroad and representative of the Local Association, and Dr. Liu Zhanen, president of Hujiang University, gave speeches in succession. The details are omitted.

Student Replies

We have our own small goals in going abroad to study. These goals are nothing more than seeking knowledge. What we seek is the new knowledge and new culture of European and American countries. What we are learning is the current situation of social services for women in Europe and America. We will apply the new knowledge and new culture to our new life in our country. We will never dare to fail your enthusiastic hopes," and so on. Wang Xiangyao and Xu Zongyi then gave replies in succession, which were largely the same, so I will not repeat them. Finally, there was a photo session, refreshments, and the meeting adjourned.

Economic Supplement

Silk and Wheat 151

— (Xinan)

"Silkworms and ripe wheat" were originally the most hopeful season for farmers, but since the continuous low prices of silkworms and wheat, farmers not only find it difficult to benefit, but in fact, they still have to suffer losses. Some people think that farmers will never do things that lose money. This is really not knowing the hardship of farming. You need to know that farmers' work is not counted as labor value. Today they plow, tomorrow they fertilize, sweat and water, they have to do it whether it's sunny or rainy. If we calculate the same way as the people in institutions, companies, stores, factories, and all those who calculate value according to labor, then the cost of one liter of wheat or one kilogram of silk, sold at market price, would probably lose 100%. Fortunately, farmers are generous and not as petty as capitalists, so no matter how low the market price is, they are always willing to sell it, and they don't complain. Next year, they will still breed as usual. In fact, farmers are not that stupid. Since they cannot avoid the exploitation of the industrial and commercial sectors, and without this, they would not even have rags and coarse food to eat, it's better to suffer a little! And in a blink of an eye, hearing the news, prices suddenly rise again. They can only blame themselves for selling too early, their fate is bad, and they can't sell at a good price, but they don't know the mystery behind it. Although this is not a definite method, the manipulation techniques have become more sophisticated over the years, and no one supervises them not to manipulate. Such situations often occur. The following will discuss silk and wheat separately.

1. Silk

Since the trend of unified control came to China, everyone talks about unified control, and silkworm cocoons cannot be an exception. Unified control is not a bad thing, but you must not think that once you talk about unified control, everything must be managed by me. Even if it should be managed, the managers must have practical experience. Don't look at anything else, just look at the foremen of the factories. If you use people who don't know what they are managing, the factory will be ruined. What's more, silkworm farming is scattered everywhere, which is more difficult to manage than a factory. You can't do it rashly. Therefore, the most important thing now is how to gradually organize them and improve the illegal aspects of their traditional breeding methods in order to increase their production and obtain favorable prices, thereby increasing their interest in silkworm farming. Considerable efforts have been made in the production of seeds, but it is only importing foreign silkworm seeds to replace local seeds. Regarding breeding methods, either the demands are too high, making farmers hesitant to approach, or they are just superficial imitations that are not suitable for farmers' actual use. China has more than 4,000 years of silkworm farming history, so it must have its advantages. Otherwise, silkworm seeds would not have spread to this day and become popular abroad. However, there are many places in the old breeding methods where they know how to do it but don't know why. Now, we should study the gains and losses of silkworm farming habits in various places and supplement their deficiencies. This is the right thing to do. It is a fact that farmers have limited knowledge, but they often use reasoning methods to breed silkworms. Someone told me that a farmer, seeing that his silkworms were about to stiffen, thought that this was like a person having a cold (what a cold is is another question). Since cold medicine is used to treat colds, why can't it be used for silkworm colds? So he mixed cold medicine water with water and sprayed it on the leaves, and the silkworms ate it and were saved. This method should not be taken as an example, and don't misunderstand that cold medicine water can cure stiff silkworms and use it for advertising. What caused them not to stiffen, and whether there are other reasons, should be discussed separately. The author mentions this because he sees that many of China's silkworm farming methods come from experience, and there must be many good methods, but they are not used properly, or should be reorganized using scientific methods. Then, guide them according to the situation and correct and improve them. Don't just bring out foreign brands. If you are really an expert, you will be able to combine the old and the new, and naturally produce a new culture or new group that adapts to the current needs, not a lifeless imitation of written knowledge.

In the past, silk merchants suffered a lot due to the falling price of silk. But now it is different. Since the price of cocoons is limited and farmers cannot sell at good prices, the price of silk has been rising year after year without being affected in the slightest. Therefore, in recent years, some silk merchants have failed and some have succeeded. But taking the interests of the majority as the interests, it is important to protect the interests of silk merchants, but the interests of farmers are also important. If we only talk about the interests of a few silk merchants and investors, and set a price to buy fresh cocoons, it's like "wanting to eat mutton but not wanting to kill sheep." This should be considered.

Since silk merchants have gained an advantage, banks have already recovered the spring cocoon loans in full. There is no need to handle autumn cocoon loans anymore, and you can imagine their complacent state. I remember during the European War, flour mills, yarn mills, and iron factories made a lot of unexpected wealth, but they used it to distribute dividends and use what came easily. What about now? The current silk industry can't even compare to one ten-thousandth of the yarn mills back then. It's just a little bit of profit, and it still comes from the price of cocoons. If their operations have surplus profits, I hope they will use it to improve mechanical equipment and develop foreign trade, rather than just focusing on distributing dividends and never planning for future business development like the factories did before. If they can do this, then although farmers have suffered losses in cocoon prices, it is still not a complete loss.

It is said that the inspection of raw silk exports has been implemented, and grading will have to wait until next year. However, from this, it can be seen that the silk industry has not yet made a sincere effort to reform itself. Speaking of raw silk inspection, as early as the 34th year of Guangxu, someone suggested establishing a raw silk inspection office in Shanghai. The Qing court only ordered the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce to invite a number of silk merchants to report to the Ministry for selection and approval. Since the founding of the Republic of China, there have been countless theories on improving raw silk, but for forty years, the situation has remained the same. Foreigners are making progress year after year and month after month, but in our country, no matter who they are, they only talk the talk. All theories are used as tools for personal gain and as a means of embellishing their image. They fail to do it in a practical way. The decline and fall are due to this. Now the silk industry is on the verge of collapse. If it is still like a swallow building its nest on a dangerous curtain, unable to pull itself together and strive for revitalization, and wants to sell silk of different grades at the same price, who would be willing to patronize it?

2. Wheat

Recently, regarding the issue of wheat exports, the grain industry and the flour industry have different positions and different views. It is reported that the Ministry of Industry and Commerce has convened a meeting to decide on the matter. Whether this is true remains to be proven by future facts.

However, it should be noted that the grain industry's claim that "wheat will rot and decay year after year" is somewhat exaggerated. And the basis of the argument is originally an estimate. According to the current situation in China, not to mention the whole country, even the production of a single place, being able to have a relatively reliable estimate, is not easy. How dare they say that the production of a certain item in a certain year is several thousand, several hundred, several tens of thousands, and that the loss is several tens of thousands, and that the planting area is several acres. I don't know what kind of survey method was used and where the estimate came from. Such actions, although it is not convenient to say that they are reckless, are also too bold. The production of industrial products is concentrated in factories, and there are records to rely on, but it is still not possible to obtain relatively reliable statistics. What about scattered and complicated agricultural products? Furthermore, such as customs import and export statistics, everyone thinks they are reliable, but they don't know how much smuggling goes in and out every year, which is not listed in the customs records. Therefore, the field of statistics is really difficult to talk about. Therefore, when compiling statistics, we should strive to be careful and ensure that the degree of credibility is one point more and better, and that the doubtful component is one point less. It is not possible to amaze people by exaggerating numbers. If the basis of statistics is unreliable, it will only confuse people. This is not the original intention of compiling statistics. Therefore, the grain industry's excuse of surplus and the flour industry's excuse of people's food are both smokescreens for business and are used for selfish purposes.

Therefore, regardless of whether wheat is surplus or insufficient, it cannot be solved by prohibiting exports. However, the time for new wheat to be harvested is not far away. Although farmers have sold some, they still have some in stock. Therefore, the price of goods will rise with the new harvest, which is beneficial to farmers. Moreover, wheat prices had already risen before the Japanese started buying, which shows that the high price of wheat is not entirely due to exports, but at most one of the reasons. The grain industry must have also hoarded a lot after seeing Japanese merchants buying, and they are afraid of the flour industry's plan to sell, so they use the excuse of abundance to argue that exports should not be prohibited, so that they can still sell at good prices. The flour industry, because the result of various parties buying up wheat at the time of new wheat production, cannot obtain cheap raw materials like in previous years, so they must find a way to make wheat prices return to normal. All these scheming maneuvers are not for the sake of people's food, nor for the sake of farmers. Therefore, if what both sides claim is true, then how to make grain cheap without hurting farmers, grain expensive without hurting the people, and how to make appropriate adjustments so that all industries have the hope of development, let's see what measures will be taken in the future.

Import of Foreign Wheat Amidst Reports of Bumper Wheat Harvests 152

— Jing Shi

Recent reports indicate that domestic wheat production has seen bumper harvests across various regions, with prices also being low. Consequently, Japanese merchants have been actively procuring wheat from the interior, already amounting to over 13,000 tons. This has caused considerable panic among mechanized flour mills, leading to a petition to the Ministry of Industry to prohibit wheat exports. Simultaneously, at this time when new wheat is entering the market, flour mills have turned to purchasing three shiploads of foreign wheat, amounting to 200,000 bags, arriving in Shanghai. While it is said that these were early orders, such a contradictory phenomenon leaves outsiders puzzled. However, based on past events, it is not surprising. We recall that in 1934, the entire country was affected by widespread drought, resulting in a significant reduction in food crop harvests. Yet, in that year, imports of foreign rice were only 7,711,000 dan, foreign wheat 4,649,000 dan, and flour 596,000 dan. In 1933, rainfall was evenly distributed across the country, leading to bountiful harvests everywhere, which in turn resulted in low grain prices that harmed farmers. The imports of foreign rice reached a staggering 12,787,000 dan, foreign wheat 10,576,000 dan, and flour 1,933,000 dan. Considering this, it is questionable whether the continuous influx of foreign grain into our country is clear evidence of domestic food shortages. However, the abnormal import of foreign grain is undoubtedly related to the scale of domestic food crop harvests and imbalances in supply and demand. Therefore, the current bumper wheat harvest and the purchase of foreign wheat are simply repeating the contradictions of the past, which is not a new phenomenon. The underlying reasons seem to be as follows:

1. Actual Shortages and Foreign Wheat Imports

Wheat production in our country is widespread; however, there are no accurate statistics available for reference on the amount produced. According to general estimates, the national output is over tens of millions of piculs. From 1931 to 1935, the average annual output was 446,339,000 piculs. This year, according to agricultural reports, the estimated harvest is over 470 million piculs, the highest predicted amount in recent years. Furthermore, the average annual import over the past five years is 11,588,970 piculs. If we add these two figures and subtract the re-exported 611,128 piculs, the total is 468,316,779 piculs. Wheat consumption is 462,435,000 piculs, which, when offset by the average annual harvest, suggests a shortage of 16,096,000 piculs (Note 1). Therefore, according to customs records, wheat imports in recent years have been 5,129,879 dan in 1932, 10,714,638 dan in 1933, 4,649,419 dan in 1934, 5,209,087 dan in 1935, and 1,117,726 dan in the first half of this year. Some of these figures are close to the calculated figures, while others exceed them. This is because wheat-producing areas in our country are vast, often located in remote areas. Even if there is a surplus, transportation is inconvenient, making it impossible to adjust for those in need. As a result, those in need feel even more deficient and have no choice but to rely on foreign wheat to supplement their needs. This is one of the reasons.

2. Flour Mills' Need for Foreign Wheat

The largest consumer of wheat is the flour milling industry. According to the Yearbook of Flour Milling, there are over 90 flour mills in the country, widely distributed across thirteen provinces. The annual output reaches 75 million bags, with a value of over 200 million yuan. The output of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui provinces is the largest, accounting for 60% of the total. Shandong and Henan provinces are next, accounting for 20%, and the remaining provinces account for the other 20%. The production and sales volume for 1934 are shown in the table below (Note 2).

According to the table above, the output in 1934 was 74,930,465 bags, with each bag weighing 49 pounds. Assuming that each picul of wheat can produce over 62 pounds of flour, the annual wheat requirement should be 44,120,745 piculs, making them the largest consumers of wheat. However, the quality of domestically produced wheat is inferior to that of foreign wheat, making it necessary to mix in foreign wheat during flour production. In addition, inconvenient transportation and high freight costs are also reasons for flour mills to use foreign wheat. For example, the freight cost per picul of Canadian wheat shipped to Shanghai is only about 60 cents in national currency, while the freight cost per picul of wheat shipped from the North China region to Shanghai is at least 80 to 90 cents. Furthermore, the cost of shipping one ton of American wheat to Shanghai, including all taxes and freight charges, is only 30 yuan, while the cost of shipping one ton of wheat from central Shaanxi to Shanghai is 130 to 140 yuan. Moreover, the wheat available in the market in our country is purely surplus from farmers' own consumption, which is then sold to the market. As a result, purchasing large quantities requires accumulating from various sources. It is not comparable to other countries, where large quantities of grain can be procured immediately. Therefore, the wheat produced in the central provinces of our country can only supply the needs of flour mills for eight months. Coupled with the time and effort required for procurement, flour mills often have to reduce or stop production to wait for supplies. As a result, it is better to directly purchase foreign wheat to reduce losses. Moreover, the shortage of raw materials for several months each year necessitates supplementation with foreign wheat. A review of customs records shows that foreign wheat is imported into ports where flour mills are concentrated, such as Tianjin, Qingdao, Shanghai, and Hankou. In practice, almost all foreign wheat imports are used to supply flour mills.

3. Price Differences Between Domestic and Foreign Wheat and Imports

Since flour mills consume a large amount of wheat each year, they are keenly aware of the importance of raw material prices and must make careful selections. The profit of flour mills depends entirely on purchasing raw materials at low prices and selling finished products at high prices. The greater the difference between the two, the greater the profit. Therefore, flour mills naturally prefer lower wheat prices on the consumption side. On the production side, they hope for rising flour prices. This is an inevitable principle for operators and needs no concealment. Therefore, the choice of flour mills to use domestic or foreign wheat depends on the prices of the two. Firstly, regarding the price comparison between foreign and domestic wheat, if the price of foreign wheat is higher than that of domestic wheat, then it is beneficial to lower the market price of wheat before it is released to the market, so that it can be purchased in large quantities, as has been the case in the past. Let us look at the market prices for the past two years:

The above figures clearly show a downward trend from May to July. Although this year's market price is higher than in previous years, the flour price is also proportional. Based on this, the import of foreign wheat seems unnecessary. It would be better to purchase domestic wheat, but instead, foreign wheat is purchased to threaten the domestic wheat market price, making it difficult to increase, and resulting in only small gains. Imports can be reduced as a result. If the difference is very small, then the profit is large, which easily promotes the import of foreign wheat. Secondly, regarding the comparison between foreign wheat and flour prices, each picul of foreign wheat can produce 80 jin of flour. If the selling price of 80 jin of flour is equal to the price of wheat, then the remaining bran and other by-products can offset the expenses other than raw materials, making it profitable. If it exceeds the wheat price, then the profit is even greater, making it worthwhile to purchase foreign wheat. Therefore, the direct purchase of foreign wheat by flour mills is not only due to whether domestic wheat production is sufficient for supply, but the key is whether it is cost-effective. Moreover, foreign agricultural products are actively commercialized, relying on political and economic support to vigorously dump them overseas, in order to achieve their desire to invade the market. Domestic agricultural products find it even more difficult to compete with them and can only watch them continuously being imported.

Moreover, producers and consumers are always in a relative position, as mentioned above. What wheat farmers hope for is to sell at a good price, which is what flour mills do not want. Conversely, farmers are unwilling for flour mills to buy wheat at low prices. However, in this era of industrial development, raw materials are often controlled by industrialists and are not independent. Even in this case, the domestic bumper harvest and foreign wheat imports are a means of manipulating market prices. Domestic wheat can only squeeze out foreign wheat in the domestic market during the autumn season, because the new crops are released on the market, and the source is very strong, and foreign wheat has no place to intervene. After that, because farmers do not have long-term storage places or are eager to sell, they are sold at the time of marketing, so the first, second, and fourth seasons are periods when both domestic and foreign wheat are handled. Only flour mills are the largest consumers of wheat, and there is this contradictory phenomenon. This is probably a measure for industrialists to manipulate raw materials, and it is another reason for foreign wheat imports.

In summary, if flour mills in our country use foreign wheat due to insufficient domestic wheat production or the need to mix in a small amount of foreign wheat for technical reasons, then it is not entirely unacceptable to purchase foreign wheat for adjustment. However, if foreign wheat is purchased in a year of bumper harvest or when new wheat is about to enter the market, then it is inevitable that there will be other motives. If so, then it will not only directly destroy the interests of farmers, but also indirectly shake the foundation of the country. As for the large-scale purchases by Japanese merchants this time, the impact on people's livelihood is significant. However, in this era of internationalization of commodities, it may be difficult to achieve results by simply prohibiting it. We only hope that flour mills and grain merchants will cooperate, take into account the interests of people's livelihood, and purchase at fair prices, so that both parties can benefit. In addition, we hope that the authorities and both producers and consumers will make further efforts to: (1) improve the quality of wheat production to meet the standards of industrial raw materials; (2) increase production to meet domestic demand; (3) reduce transportation costs as much as possible to facilitate agricultural transportation; (4) establish more warehouses to prepare for longer-term storage; and (5) balance market prices to avoid speculative manipulation. If these aspects can be implemented step by step, then the entire issue of people's livelihood can be easily resolved, not just wheat alone. Note 1: See "New Estimates of Food Supply and Demand in China" in International Trade Journal, Volume 8, Issue 6. Note 2: 1936 Shen Bao Yearbook, Flour Milling Industry, 8.14.

What are the Reasons for the Gradual Decline in Mulberry Fields? 153

— Li Yinbei

Rice, wheat, cotton, silk, and tea are the foundation of our country's agricultural products. Among them, silk farming greatly benefits the circulation of the rural economy. However, since 1930, silkworm farming has not only been unprofitable for farmers, but also a burden that has resulted in losses. As a result, they have been removing mulberry trees that provide food for silkworms and planting other crops instead. Although we do not currently have accurate statistics for research, we can infer the general situation of the remaining mulberry fields in recent years by extrapolating from the decline in raw silk production. The following table lists the export trade of seven types of raw silk in the last five years (unit: dan).

Raw silk is a major commodity in our country's foreign trade. Apart from a small number of silk mills in the interior, the domestic market mainly depends on the sales situation of foreign firms. Although we cannot absolutely say that the gradual decline in raw silk export trade is the sole cause of the reduction in mulberry fields, we cannot deny that the gradual decline in raw silk figures reflects the decrease in the number of silkworms raised by silkworm farmers. This is an undeniable fact. As the number of silkworms raised by silkworm farmers decreases, the mulberry fields become oversupplied. If we further base our calculations on the feeding capacity of mulberry fields in Jiangsu Province, each mu of mulberry field can feed silkworms that produce eight jin of fresh cocoons (see Shanghai Current Affairs News on June 14, 1935, "The Sericulture Industry in Jiangsu Province"). Assuming that the silk reeling rate is 500 jin and the dry folding rate is 300, then producing one dan of raw silk requires 18.75 mu of mulberry field.——(One dan of raw silk × 500 reeling rate × 300 drying rate × 100 jin / 80 jin of fresh cocoons = 18.75 mu) Based on this calculation, the supply and demand situation of mulberry fields in recent years is as follows:

Since 1931, the leaves produced by mulberry fields have shown an increasing oversupply. In order to generate income from the surplus mulberry fields, silkworm farmers often remove the surplus mulberry fields and plant other crops instead. This situation is most prevalent in Wuxi and Jintan in Jiangsu, and Huzhou and Hangzhou in Zhejiang. This is mainly because the people in these rural areas rely on silkworm farming and mulberry planting as their main industries. Once the price of raw silk plummets, the number of silkworm farmers decreases sharply, resulting in significant losses from the surplus mulberry fields! Therefore, they have no choice but to plant rice and wheat to make up for the losses.

Next, what are the reasons for the silkworm farmers to abandon mulberry planting and switch to other crops? We can discuss this from the following three aspects:

(A) The Progress of Social Culture and the Transformation of Raw Silk Consumption. This is the fundamental reason for the movement of silkworm farmers abandoning mulberry planting and switching to other crops. It is found that the sales of raw silk in our country are mainly to the United States and France. However, since the invention of artificial silk, people around the world have undergone a remarkable shift in the production, promotion, and consumption of artificial silk. Among them, consumers have developed considerable confidence in artificial silk. Looking at the current silk fabrics, it is already impossible to demand purely raw silk woven products. On the weaving mill side, it is not an attempt to cut corners, but rather that consumers are psychologically pleased with the luster of artificial silk. This is a metabolism of the entire culture, which we cannot reverse. The International Silk Guild Inc. (established in August 1933 by the United States silk industry giants Qian Li and others, with the general office in New York) is a powerful organization for reviving raw silk promotion. However, it cannot use negative criticism to publicize the effect of artificial silk on consumers' psychology. In her inaugural declaration, she said: "In recent years, the silk industry, which has always been prosperous, has been completely invaded by artificial silk! Weaving factories are unwilling to initiate sponsoring publicity for any party because raw silk and artificial silk are used together. However, a few silk weavers still believe that the American raw silk industry should not be afraid of difficulties and should strive to develop raw silk: As for producing countries such as Japan, Italy, and China, they should cooperate with the American raw silk promotion groups. Efforts should be made to re-impress the advantages of raw silk into the minds of ordinary customers." Moreover, the more advanced science is, the more amazing inventions there will be: according to the Shanghai Financial Industry Report on December 6, 1933, the Japanese Fuji Silk Company is about to engage in the manufacture of "recycled silk." It is found that Ranxin Silk is a silk quality that Japanese people have painstakingly researched and successfully replaced artificial silk due to the lack of raw materials for artificial silk in their own country. The manufacturing method is to wash, bleach, and dissolve old silk or silk cocoon scraps using chemical methods, and then make them into silk using the method of manufacturing artificial silk. Therefore, the Japanese call it recycled silk. It is expected that once this silk comes out, it will add another kind of encroachment and crowding out to the future of raw silk.

(B) The Lagging Man-Made Economic Status. Secondly, the lagging man-made economic status is also a powerful reason. The lagging man-made economic status leads to the lagging international economic status. It must be known that raw silk is a commodity in the international market, and it is closely related to a country's politics, currency system, trade, and exchange rates. Our country is in a quasi-colonial status; every move is bound by others – in recent facts, due to the stability of exchange rates, export silk warp is more active than before.

(C) Silk costs, cocoon costs, and silkworm costs cannot be connected. In theory, the price of silk and cocoons is completely linked to the cost of silkworms. But the actual situation is not like this. Most surprisingly, the silkworm farmer's income and the factory's expenses are often not rationally aligned. This situation is caused by the current poor cocoon collection methods. It is found that the current method of collection is mostly entrusted by factories to village cocoon shops for collection. The expenses are so great that they are greater than any other industry. Therefore, even if factories spend a lot of money, it is difficult for them to purely flow into the hands of silkworm farmers.

We understand the root causes of this de-mulberry movement, so what is the future direction of planting mulberry and switching crops? Although this year's raw silk market price has improved slightly, and the price of fresh cocoons has increased compared to previous years, the difference from the silkworm farmer's cost is still huge. For example, when the spring fresh cocoon market opened in Wuxi, silkworm farmers in groups and teams went to various parties to petition, with the main goal of taking care of silkworm costs and striving for it. In other places, the same thing may be happening. Therefore, it is speculated that this de-mulberry movement is naturally lurking in rural villages everywhere and cannot be said to have been eliminated. For the sake of the current plan: on the passive side, we must plan to promote the cultivation of improved mulberry varieties to enhance their feeding capacity. On the active side, we must promote silkworm farming production cooperatives, especially focusing on the promotion of joint drying and selling, so as to replace the uneconomical cocoon collection by cocoon shops. All of these things, both directly and indirectly, are of great help to the mulberry retention problem.

The Process of Silkworm Farmers in Wuxi Self-Drying Cocoons 154

— Wang Liangfeng

Since the implementation of the control of the silkworm farming industry in Wuxi, the variety, price, purchase, distribution, and management of silkworm eggs, cocoon shop collection, collection of improvement fees, and silkworm farming guidance have all had significant results. This spring (1936), the Wuxi Silkworm Farming Model Area and the Wuxi Farmers Bank have made efforts to promote self-drying cocoons by silkworm farmers, which has been quite effective. Since the implementation of legal tender in our country, the overseas exchange market has seen a leveling off, and the silk price conversion can be extremely volatile. Since the first half of 1935, the economic situation in the United States has gradually turned around, so the silk price has continued to rise, exports have increased, and the future has shown promise. Fresh cocoons are the agricultural products of farmers. In order to maintain production costs, farmers should have a price-setting position. If you want to have a price-setting position, you can only achieve it by drying fresh cocoons into dry cocoons. This spring, Wuxi has organized a large-scale cocoon collection company, hoping to monopolize the price of products, which may inevitably be manipulated and suppressed. This is especially important for farmers to dry cocoons themselves.

In order to facilitate farmers' self-drying cocoons, and to actively implement it, Jiangsu Province has specially formulated implementation methods for promoting cooperative silkworm production. On March 24, 1936, it was passed by the provincial government and ordered the Wuxi County Mayor to be the director of the Silkworm Farming Model Area, together with cooperative instructors, to use the central silkworm farming guidance center as a basis to guide silkworm farmers to organize business. Local people automatically organized more than 50 silkworm farming cooperatives, plus the original 20-plus production and marketing cooperatives, for a total of more than 80. All locations have been distributed throughout the county, so silkworm farmers' self-drying cocoons have a considerable organization.

Cooperative cocoon drying first needs to have cocoon stoves. If they are allowed to build them on their own, there may be difficulties in terms of economy and time. Therefore, the implementation methods for cooperative silkworm production stipulates that any cocoon shops and silkworm farming joint societies that have been approved by the model area to open the market have priority in renting them. However, this method has some difficulties in fact and environment. There are many single stoves in Wuxi rural areas that are less than four by four. For the sake of taking care of everything, the provincial government specially allows cooperatives to buy the cocoon stoves that should be banned and use them for members to dry cocoons. In various cocoon shops, they can turn useless into useful, and in various cooperatives, they can also get suitable cocoon stoves. It is also stipulated that if cooperatives lack funds, they are allowed to temporarily rent them before they are purchased. This spring, the Wuxi County Silkworm Farming Model Area approved a total of 47 cocoon shops for cooperatives to rent. (Several cooperatives use one cocoon shop, so the number of cocoon shops is less than the number of cooperative societies.) A total of 130 single stoves and 4 double stoves were opened. Among them, 6 are qualified cocoon shops, and the rest are unqualified cocoon shops that have been sealed.

In order to support the cooperatives' cocoon drying, the Wuxi Farmers Bank also specially signed a silk cocoon bank and formulated methods for accepting cooperative self-drying cocoons and lending drying expenses. If various cooperatives feel that they lack funds when operating cocoon drying and sales, the persons in charge of each cooperative can borrow from the bank. The following is an excerpt of the method. (1) Any dry cocoons that cooperative members jointly dry can borrow money from the bank, but they must meet the following conditions:

A, The dry cocoons must be piled into the silk cocoon warehouse designated by the bank.

B, The cocoon body is good;

C, The degree of drying is uniform and appropriate;

D, Must be determined by the person in charge of the cooperative to the bank; (1) The mortgage price is 60% of the market price; (1) The mortgage period is up to five months; (1) The interest rate is 9/1000 per month, calculated daily; (1) Any cooperative may borrow from the bank for the drying expenses required for baking fresh cocoons, but it must be handled in accordance with the following articles: A, When applying for a loan, the number of dry cocoons baked by the members must be estimated first, and the bank's investigation must be confirmed;

B, Each dry cocoon is allowed to borrow 6 yuan in national currency;

C, The loan period is up to one month;

D, The interest rate is 9/1000 per month, calculated daily;

Looking at the cooperative, from drying cocoons to finance, they have received considerable assistance, and everything can be carried out smoothly.

This spring, there is no survey statistics on the number of cocoons dried by the various cooperatives. However, it can be estimated from the improvement fees paid by the cooperatives. As of the end of August, the cooperatives in the county paid a total of 9,431 yuan in improvement fees. Calculating the improvement fee of 4.5 yuan per dry cocoon, it can be seen that a total of 2,096 dry cocoons were dried. Estimating that the maximum number of fresh cocoons is 200 jin per dry cocoon, the estimated number of fresh cocoons is 6,288 dan. Calculated by the total improvement fee of 210,000 yuan in the county, the number of self-dried cocoons only accounts for 4.4% of the county. The number is extremely small and needs to be promoted. It is also found that this spring's tear price in Wuxi County was 11 yuan. Since the spring cocoon has a love market, the price overseas has frequently risen, and the dry cocoon market price has also risen accordingly. Each dry cocoon (old silk) can be sold for 170 yuan, which is equivalent to 140 yuan per market. Each cooperative followed up with the sale of dry cocoons at any time, calculating that it could add more than 10 yuan per ancestral home compared to selling fresh cocoons. From the time the fresh cocoons go on the market to the sale of dry cocoons, it took less than two months, and the increase in income for silkworm farmers in the cocoon baking was a total of more than 60,000 yuan, which is no small amount.

Statistics show that a total of 12 cooperatives deposited their self-dried cocoons with the Wuxi Farmers Bank, depositing more than 280 ancestral cocoons, with a total outstanding mortgage of more than 22,000 yuan, accounting for 1.8% of the total number of self-dried cocoons. All those who apply for bank mortgages for use are jointly transported and sold. Those who do not apply for mortgages take back and sell in retail after baking. The entire collective action is still lacking, and more attention should be paid in the future. Those who jointly bake should be based on the principle of joint sales, so as to avoid the exploitation of middlemen.

This spring, all farmers who dry their own cocoons have made a profit. In my opinion, it is proposed that a considerable percentage of the profits be withdrawn as a public reserve fund to be used for improving silkworm farming, or as a foundation for building cocoon stoves, or to offset accidental losses. If this public reserve fund can be withdrawn on time, the number will accumulate more and more, and the foundation will become more and more solid. It is extremely important for the baking and transport business and cannot be ignored.
